But once you enter, you are taken away to a different place. Inside you‚Äôll find a coffee shop, with pastries and cakes and cookies. Lots of seating and comfortable nooks and crannies to sit and read some of the magazines they have, or your favorite book.

They also have group tables if you‚Äôre feeling a little social. If the fresh baked goods aren‚Äôt your thing, they have a few fridges full of food and snacks and other goodies.

This place reminds me of the old school markets and coffee shops where the neighborhood would come to meet, and chat, socialize and enjoy a cup of tea or coffee.

In regards to the coffee, I have to be honest, it was terrible. I think maybe it was a little old or something,¬†¬†it was bitter and kind of sour. Double charged me for drinks. Explained the situation to the bartender AND the manager, whom both refused to believe what ACTUALLY happened.

I would give this place negative 20 stars if I could for the attitude that came with it. Atrocious customer service. And that was on my first drink of the night.

Details:
Friend: (to the bartender) can I get a Long Island (for herself) and a margarita(for me)?
Bartender: *gives us our drinks*
Me: *gives him a credit card to pay for my drink (margarita)*
Bartender: open or close?
Me: open for now, thanks.
Friend: *orders a beer for another friend*
Bartender: $8
Friend: oh I'm paying for the beer and this Long Island
Bartender: okay *rings up the new total* open or close?
Friend: close
- about an hour later -
Me: can I close my tab?
Bartender: *hands me the tab*
Me: $20 for one drink?
Bartender: you got two drinks
Me: no, my friend paid for hers separately. I only got the one drink
Bartender: no, I gave you two drinks. I remember
Me: um NO that's not what happened
Bartender: you can bring your friend here to clear this up
Me: this is bs. *finds friend and brings her to the bar*
Friend: *explains that she paid for her drink separately to the bartender*
Bartender: *to my friend* no, I gave her two drinks. *to me* What I charged you is what I charged you. Can't fix it.
Me: can I speak to a manager??
-- The bartender and the manager talk with each other before the manager comes up to us. We explain to him the situation and he tries to tell us that he spoke to the bartenders and that my friend paid for a totally random drink (which we did NOT get) on a separate tab. What???? ARE YOU KIDDING ME???

Save yourself the trouble; go somewhere else. Unbelievable!!

P.S. I have NEVER argued with a server/management like this before. Probably because other people KNOW HOW TO DO THEIR JOB RIGHT. Also, upon reading other reviews, overcharging and horrible customer service seems to be a reoccurring theme at this place</Review>

< Text>
A few things I notice at just about every Auld is that that it's where non Irish go to drink like their Irish. It's also a place that is surprisingly sportsbarish. The olden triangle (5/405/55) is not known for having basr, places to drink, party or be merry. Much of Irvine is super business park corporate area and people need to unwind and do it locally, so it's no wonder Auld is a bit of a hotspot. Is it me or every Auld I tend to hangout the furthest from the bathroom and find it annoying having to walk so far? Not that I do it on purpose, but I go where the ladies go. Maybe there is a correlation. A nice selection of beers, but not like the booming craftropolis' we have down in San Diego. Food is a step up from TGIF and what any real man looks for is Scotch, single malts and Whiskey (not the usuals). Ladies can still get their fruity drinks and the waitress' are surprisingly good, maybe not the friendliest, but hey they come around and take even my quirkiest drink orders verbatim. A surprisingly older crowd than the LB location, but hey isn't that the nature of Long Beach vs. Irvine. I guess there is a lot of regulars and I'm not yet one of them. They come back time and time again and I don't know why. If there was a divebar closer to my office than this I'd be there, but until then it's less upscale than it's neighbors. Do with what you got. The food is ok, but if you're coming here to eat vs. sop up booze you're in the wrong place< /Text>

< text>
Great food and cocktails in a pleasant dining room, with good service. We had the squid ink Campanelle, the seared scallops, and the sea bass special. All were excellent. < review>
The experience at Lure + Till was a bit confusing, but thankfully also delicious.
The drinks on the drinks menu looked a bit too strong for my friend and I, so we asked for a mojito and orange aperol and they were simply delightful.
The menu was a bit confusing - we had to look up about 12 different things.  Our server was kinda helpful, albeit a little awkward.
Oysters on the half shell were fresh, and the mignonette that came with was light and added just the right amount of acidity.
My friend's Charcuterie plate was large enough for 2 (possibly 4).  High quality bread and the mustard dipping things were a perfect compliment to the prosciutto and bologna (?).
My friend had the watercress salad, which was presented as a beautiful garden with flowers on top.
My squid ink campanelli with lobster was rich and flavorful.
The cherry and apricot tart with sugared pistachio was the perfect end to our meal - sweet yet airy, creamy but somehow dairy-free.
I'm looking forward to returning to Lure + Till.<//review>
